4792 <section id="_687">

4793

4794 <h2>

4795Treatment of Recurrent Adult CNS Tumors</h2>

4796

4797 <div id="_section_687" class="pdq-sections">

4798<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4799<h6>

4800In This Section</h6>

4801<ul>

4802<li>

4803<a href="#_961_toc">

4804Chemotherapy<ul>

4805<li>

4806<a href="#_977_toc">

4807Localized chemotherapy (carmustine wafer)</a>

4808</li>

4809<li>

4810<a href="#_692_toc">

4811Systemic chemotherapy</a>

4812</li>

4813</ul>

4814</a>

4815</li>

4816<li>

4817<a href="#_976_toc">

4818Antiangiogenesis Therapy</a>

4819</li>

4820<li>

4821<a href="#_694_toc">

4822Radiation Therapy</a>

4823</li>

4824<li>

4825<a href="#_1228_toc">

4826Surgery</a>

4827</li>

4828<li>

4829<a href="#_TrialSearch_687_sid_7_toc">

4830Current Clinical Trials</a>

4831</li>

4832</ul>

4833</nav>

4834<p id="_1223" tabindex="-1">

4835Patients who have recurrent CNS tumors are rarely curable and should consider enrollment in clinical trials. Information about ongoing clinical trials is available from the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials">

4836NCI website</a>

4837.</p>

4838<p id="_990" tabindex="-1">

4839Standard treatment options for recurrent CNS tumors include the following:</p>

4840<div class="pdq-content-list">

4841<ol id="_991">

4842<li>

4843<a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_961">

4844Chemotherapy</a>

4845.</li>

4846<li>

4847<a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_976">

4848Antiangiogenesis therapy</a>

4849.</li>

4850<li>

4851<a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_694">

4852Radiation therapy</a>

4853.</li>

4854<li>

4855<a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_1228">

4856Surgery</a>

4857.</li>

4858</ol>

4859</div>

4860<section id="_961">

4861<h3 id="_961_toc">

4862Chemotherapy</h3>

4863<section id="_977">

4864<h4 id="_977_toc">

4865Localized chemotherapy (carmustine wafer)</h4>

4866<p id="_691" tabindex="-1">

4867Carmustine wafers have been investigated for the treatment of recurrent malignant gliomas, but the impact on survival is less clear than at the time of initial diagnosis and resection. </p>

4868<p id="_1020" tabindex="-1">

4869Evidence (localized chemotherapy):</p>

4870<div class="pdq-content-list">

4871<ol id="_1021">

4872<li>

4873In a multicenter randomized, placebo-controlled trial, 222 patients with recurrent malignant primary brain tumors requiring reoperation were randomly assigned to receive implanted carmustine wafers or placebo biodegradable wafers.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

48741</a>

4875][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4876Level of evidence A1</a>

4877] Approximately half of the patients had received previous systemic chemotherapy. The two treatment groups were well balanced at baseline. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4878<ul id="_1224">

4879<li>

4880Median survival was 31 weeks in the group receiving carmustine wafers versus 23 weeks in the group receiving placebo wafers. The statistical significance between the two overall survival curves depended on the method of analysis. </li>

4881<li>

4882The hazard ratio (HR) for risk of dying in the direct intention-to-treat comparison between the two groups was 0.83 (95% confidence interval [CI], 0.63&#8211;1.10; <em>

4883P </em>

4884 = .19). The baseline characteristics were similar in the two groups, but the investigators performed an additional analysis, adjusting for prognostic factors, because they felt that even small differences in baseline characteristics could have a powerful influence on outcomes. In the adjusted proportional hazards model, the HR for risk of death was 0.67 (95% CI, 0.51&#8211;0.90, <em>

4885P</em>

4886 = .006). The investigators emphasized this latter analysis and reported this as a positive trial.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

48871</a>

4888][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4889Level of evidence A1</a>

4890]</li>

4891</ul>

4892</div>

4893</li>

4894<li>

4895A Cochrane Collaboration systematic review of chemotherapeutic wafers for high-grade glioma focused on the unadjusted analysis and reported the same trial as negative.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

48962</a>

4897]</li>

4898</ol>

4899</div>

4900</section>

4901<section id="_692">

4902<h4 id="_692_toc">

4903Systemic chemotherapy</h4>

4904<p id="_920" tabindex="-1">

4905Systemic therapy (e.g., temozolomide, lomustine, or the combination of procarbazine, a nitrosourea, and vincristine (PCV) in patients who have not previously received the drugs) has been used at the time of recurrence of primary malignant brain tumors. However, this approach has not been tested in controlled studies. Patient-selection factors likely play a strong role in determining outcomes, so the impact of therapy on survival is not clear.</p>

4906</section>

4907</section>

4908<section id="_976">

4909<h3 id="_976_toc">

4910Antiangiogenesis Therapy</h3>

4911<p id="_916" tabindex="-1">

4912In 2009, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) granted accelerated approval of bevacizumab monotherapy for patients with progressive glioblastoma. The indication was granted under the FDA&#8217;s accelerated approval program that permits the use of certain surrogate end points or an effect on a clinical end point other than survival or irreversible morbidity as bases for approvals of products intended for serious or life-threatening illnesses or conditions. </p>

4913<p id="_1225" tabindex="-1">

4914The approval was based on the demonstration of improved objective response rates observed in two historically controlled, single-arm, or noncomparative phase II trials.[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

49153</a>

4916,<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

49174</a>

4918][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4919Level of evidence C3</a>

4920] On the basis of these data and FDA approval, bevacizumab monotherapy has become standard therapy for recurrent glioblastoma.</p>

4921<p id="_1022" tabindex="-1">

4922Evidence (antiangiogenesis therapy):</p>

4923<div class="pdq-content-list">

4924<ol id="_1023">

4925<li>

4926The FDA independently reviewed an open-label, multicenter, noncomparative phase II study that randomly assigned 167 recurrent glioblastoma multiforme (GBM) patients to receive bevacizumab alone or bevacizumab in combination with irinotecan,[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

49273</a>

4928] although only efficacy data from the bevacizumab monotherapy arm (n = 85) were used to support drug approval. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4929<ul id="_1226">

4930<li>

4931Tumor responses were observed in 26% of patients treated with bevacizumab alone, and the median duration of response in these patients was 4.2 months. </li>

4932<li>

4933On the basis of this externally controlled trial, the incidence of adverse events associated with bevacizumab did not appear to be significantly increased in GBM patients. </li>

4934</ul>

4935</div>

4936</li>

4937<li>

4938The FDA independently assessed another single-arm, single-institution trial in which 56 recurrent glioblastoma patients were treated with bevacizumab alone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

49394</a>

4940] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4941<ul id="_1227">

4942<li>

4943Responses were observed in 20% of patients, and the median duration of response was 3.9 months.</li>

4944</ul>

4945</div>

4946</li>

4947</ol>

4948</div>

4949<p id="_918" tabindex="-1">

4950No data are available from prospective, randomized controlled trials demonstrating improvement in health outcomes, such as disease-related symptoms or increased survival with the use of bevacizumab to treat glioblastoma. </p>

4951</section>

4952<section id="_694">

4953<h3 id="_694_toc">

4954Radiation Therapy</h3>

4955<p id="_695" tabindex="-1">

4956Because there are no randomized trials, the role of repeat radiation after disease progression or the development of radiation-induced cancers is also ill defined. Interpretation is difficult because the literature is limited to small retrospective case series.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

49575</a>

4958] The decision must be made carefully because of the risk of neurocognitive deficits and radiation necrosis.</p>

4959</section>

4960<section id="_1228">

4961<h3 id="_1228_toc">

4962Surgery</h3>

4963<p id="_1229" tabindex="-1">

4964Re-resection of recurrent CNS tumors is used for some patients. However, most patients do not qualify because of a deteriorating condition or technically inoperable tumors. The evidence is limited to noncontrolled studies and case series of patients who are healthy enough and have tumors that are small enough to technically debulk. The impact on survival of reoperation versus patient selection is not known.</p>

4965</section>

4966<section id="_TrialSearch_687_sid_7">

4967<h3 id="_TrialSearch_687_sid_7_toc">

4968Current Clinical Trials</h3>

4969<p id="_TrialSearch_687_22" tabindex="-1">

4970Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

4971advanced clinical trial search</a>

4972 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

4973General information</a>

4974 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4975</section>

5009Changes to This Summary (01/20/2023)</h2>

5010

5011 <div id="_section_233" class="pdq-sections">

5012<p id="_1359" tabindex="-1">

5013The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as

5014new information becomes available. This section describes the latest

5015changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

5016<p id="_1409" tabindex="-1">

5017<strong>

5018<a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_1">

5019General Information About Adult Central Nervous System Tumors</a>

5020</strong>

5021</p>

5022<p id="_1410" tabindex="-1">

5023Updated <a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_933">

5024statistics</a>

5025 with estimated new cases and deaths for 2023 (cited American Cancer Society as reference 2).</p>

5026<p id="_1411" tabindex="-1">

5027Updated <a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_935">

5028text</a>

5029 about incidence and mortality rates.</p>

5030<p id="_disclaimerHP_3" tabindex="-1">

5031This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

5032PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5033, which is

5034editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

5035the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

5036information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

5037maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

5038About This PDQ Summary</a>

5039 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

5040PDQ&#174; Cancer Information for Health Professionals</a>

5041 pages.

5049 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

5050

5051 <h2>

5052About This PDQ Summary</h2>

5053

5054 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

5055<section id="_AboutThis_2">

5056<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

5057Purpose of This Summary</h3>

5058<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

5059This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of adult central nervous system tumors. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

5060</section>

5061<section id="_AboutThis_4">

5062<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

5063Reviewers and Updates</h3>

5064<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

5065This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

5066PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5067, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

5068<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

5069 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

5070<div class="pdq-content-list">

5071<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

5072<li>

5073be discussed at a meeting,</li>

5074<li>

5075be cited with text, or</li>

5076<li>

5077replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

5078</ul>

5079</div>

5080<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

5081Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

5082<p id="" tabindex="-1">

5083The lead reviewer for Adult Central Nervous System Tumors Treatment is:</p>

5084<div class="pdq-content-list">

5085<ul id="">

5086<li>

5087Minh Tam Truong, MD (Boston University Medical Center)</li>

5088</ul>

5089</div>

5090<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

5091Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

5092Email Us</a>

5093. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

5094</section>

5095<section id="_AboutThis_10">

5096<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

5097Levels of Evidence</h3>

5098<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

5099Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

5100formal evidence ranking system</a>

5101 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

5102</section>

5103<section id="_AboutThis_12">

5104<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

5105Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

5106<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

5107PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

5108<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

5109The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

5110<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

5111PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Adult Central Nervous System Tumors Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq">

5112https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/adult-brain-treatment-pdq</a>

5113. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389419]</p>

5114<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

5115Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

5116Visuals Online</a>

5117, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

5118

5119</p>

5120</section>

5123Disclaimer</h3>

5125Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

5126Managing Cancer Care</a>

5127 page.</p>
